	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>Encyclopædia Britannica</i></h1>

<p>The <b><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i></b> (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for "British Encyclopaedia"), formerly published by <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica,_Inc." title="Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.">Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.</a>, is a <a href="/wiki/General_knowledge" title="General knowledge">general knowledge</a> <a href="/wiki/English-language" class="mw-redirect" title="English-language">English-language</a> <a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia" title="Encyclopedia">encyclopaedia</a>. It was written by about 100&#160;full-time editors and more than 4,000&#160;contributors. The 2010 version of the 15th edition, which spans 32 volumes<sup id="cite_ref-nytstop_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytstop-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and 32,640 pages, was the last printed edition.
</p><p>The <i>Britannica</i> is the English-language encyclopaedia that was in print for the longest time: it lasted 244 years. It was first published between 1768 and 1771 in the <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scottish</a> capital of <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, as three volumes. (This first edition is available in facsimile.) The encyclopaedia grew in size: the second edition was 10 volumes,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and by its fourth edition (1801–1810) it had expanded to 20 volumes.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Its rising stature as a scholarly work helped recruit eminent contributors, and the 9th (1875–1889) and <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica_Eleventh_Edition" title="Encyclopædia Britannica Eleventh Edition">11th editions</a> (1911) are landmark encyclopaedias for scholarship and literary style. Beginning with the 11th edition and following its acquisition by an American firm, the <i>Britannica</i> shortened and simplified articles to broaden its appeal to the <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North American</a> market. In 1933, the <i>Britannica</i> became the first encyclopaedia to adopt "continuous revision", in which the encyclopaedia is continually reprinted, with every article updated on a schedule<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. In March 2012, Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc. announced it would no longer publish printed editions, and would focus instead on <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica_Online" title="Encyclopædia Britannica Online">Encyclopædia Britannica Online</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 15th edition had a three-part structure: a 12-volume <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Microp%C3%A6dia" title="Micropædia">Micropædia</a></i> of short articles (generally fewer than 750&#160;words), a 17-volume <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Macrop%C3%A6dia" title="Macropædia">Macropædia</a></i> of long articles (two to 310&#160;pages), and a single <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Prop%C3%A6dia" title="Propædia">Propædia</a></i> volume to give a <a href="/wiki/Hierarchical" class="mw-redirect" title="Hierarchical">hierarchical</a> outline of knowledge. The <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> was meant for quick fact-checking and as a guide to the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i>; readers are advised to study the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Propædia</i> outline to understand a subject's context and to find more detailed articles. Over 70 years, the size of the <i>Britannica</i> has remained steady, with about 40&#160;million words on half a million topics. Though published in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> since 1901, the <i>Britannica</i> has for the most part maintained <a href="/wiki/American_and_British_English_spelling_differences" title="American and British English spelling differences">British English spelling</a>.
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Present_status">Present status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Present status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Print_version">Print version</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Print version">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Encyclopaedia_Britannica_15_with_2002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Encyclopaedia_Britannica_15_with_2002.jpg/250px-Encyclopaedia_Britannica_15_with_2002.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Encyclopaedia_Britannica_15_with_2002.jpg/375px-Encyclopaedia_Britannica_15_with_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Encyclopaedia_Britannica_15_with_2002.jpg/500px-Encyclopaedia_Britannica_15_with_2002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="776" data-file-height="739" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Encyclopaedia_Britannica_15_with_2002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>15th edition of the <i>Britannica</i>. The initial volume with the green spine is the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Prop%C3%A6dia" title="Propædia">Propædia</a></i>; the red-spined and black-spined volumes are the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Microp%C3%A6dia" title="Micropædia">Micropædia</a></i> and the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Macrop%C3%A6dia" title="Macropædia">Macropædia</a></i>, respectively. The last three volumes are the 2002 Book of the Year (black spine) and the two-volume index (cyan spine).</div></div></div>
<p>Since 1985, the <i>Britannica</i> has had four parts: the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Microp%C3%A6dia" title="Micropædia">Micropædia</a></i>, the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Macrop%C3%A6dia" title="Macropædia">Macropædia</a></i>, the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Prop%C3%A6dia" title="Propædia">Propædia</a></i>, and a two-volume index. The <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> articles are found in the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micro-</i> and <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i>, which encompass 12 and 17 volumes, respectively, each volume having roughly one thousand pages. The 2007 <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i> has 699 in-depth articles, ranging in length from 2 to 310 pages and having references and named contributors. In contrast, the 2007 <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> has roughly 65,000 articles, the vast majority (about 97%) of which contain fewer than 750 words, no references, and no named contributors.<sup id="cite_ref-library_association_1996_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-library_association_1996-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> articles are intended for quick fact-checking and to help in finding more thorough information in the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i>. The <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i> articles are meant both as authoritative, well-written articles on their subjects and as storehouses of information not covered elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The longest article (310 pages) is on the United States, and resulted from the merger of the articles on the individual states. The 2013 edition of <i>Britannica</i> contained approximately forty thousand articles.<sup id="cite_ref-store.britannica.com_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-store.britannica.com-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Information can be found in the <i>Britannica</i> by following the cross-references in the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> and <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i>; however, these are sparse, averaging one cross-reference per page.<sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Hence, readers are recommended to consult instead the alphabetical index or the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Propædia</i>, which organizes the <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> contents by topic.<sup id="cite_ref-index_preface_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index_preface-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The core of the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Propædia</i> is its "Outline of Knowledge", which aims to provide a logical framework for all human knowledge.<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_preface_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_preface-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Accordingly, the Outline is consulted by the <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> editors to decide which articles should be included in the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micro-</i> and <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_preface_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_preface-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The Outline is also intended to be a study guide, to put subjects in their proper perspective, and to suggest a series of <i>Britannica</i> articles for the student wishing to learn a topic in depth.<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_preface_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_preface-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> However, libraries have found that it is scarcely used, and reviewers have recommended that it be dropped from the encyclopaedia.<sup id="cite_ref-library_association_1992_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-library_association_1992-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Propædia</i> also has color transparencies of human anatomy and several appendices listing the staff members, advisors, and contributors to all three parts of the <i>Britannica</i>.
</p><p>Taken together, the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> and <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i> comprise roughly 40 million words and 24,000 images.<sup id="cite_ref-index_preface_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index_preface-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The two-volume index has 2,350 pages, listing the 228,274 topics covered in the <i>Britannica</i>, together with 474,675 subentries under those topics.<sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Britannica</i> generally prefers <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British spelling</a> over <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> for example, it uses <i>colour</i> (not <i>color</i>), <i>centre</i> (not <i>center</i>), and <i>encyclopaedia</i> (not <i>encyclopedia</i>). However, there are exceptions to this rule, such as <i>defense</i> rather than <i>defence</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Common alternative spellings are provided with cross-references such as "Color: <i>see</i> Colour."
</p><p>Since 1936, the articles of the <i>Britannica</i> have been revised on a regular schedule, with at least 10% of them considered for revision each year.<sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-encyclopaedia_1954_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopaedia_1954-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> According to one Britannica website, 46% of its articles were revised over the past three years;<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> however, according to another Britannica web-site, only 35% of the articles were revised.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The alphabetization of articles in the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> and <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i> follows strict rules.<sup id="cite_ref-micropedia_preface_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-micropedia_preface-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">Diacritical</a> marks and non-English letters are ignored, while numerical entries such as "<a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">1812, War of</a>" are alphabetized as if the number had been written out ("Eighteen-twelve, War of"). Articles with identical names are ordered first by persons, then by places, then by things. Rulers with identical names are organized first alphabetically by country and then by chronology; thus, <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Simple" title="Charles the Simple">Charles III</a> of France precedes <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I of England</a>, listed in <i>Britannica</i> as the ruler of Great Britain and Ireland. (That is, they are alphabetized as if their titles were "Charles, France, 3" and "Charles, Great Britain and Ireland, 1".) Similarly, places that share names are organized alphabetically by country, then by ever-smaller political divisions.
</p><p>In March 2012, the company announced that the 2010 edition would be the last printed version. This was announced as a move by the company to adapt to the times and focus on its future using digital distribution.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The peak year for the printed encyclopaedia was 1990 when 120,000 sets were sold, but it dropped to 40,000 in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> 12,000 sets of the 2010 edition were printed, of which 8,000 had been sold as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> By late April 2012, the remaining copies of the 2010 edition had sold out at Britannica's online store. As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, a replica of Britannica's 1768 first edition is sold on the online store.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_printed_material">Related printed material</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Related printed material">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Britannica Junior</i> was first published in 1934 as 12 volumes. It was expanded to 15 volumes in 1947, and renamed <i>Britannica Junior Encyclopædia</i> in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> It was taken off the market after the 1984 printing.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Children%27s_Britannica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Children%27s_Britannica.jpg/250px-Children%27s_Britannica.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Children%27s_Britannica.jpg/375px-Children%27s_Britannica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Children%27s_Britannica.jpg/500px-Children%27s_Britannica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="980" data-file-height="526" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Children%27s_Britannica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Children's Britannica</i></div></div></div>
<p>A British <i>Children's Britannica</i> edited by <a href="/wiki/John_Armitage_(editor)" title="John Armitage (editor)">John Armitage</a> was issued in London in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Its contents were determined largely by the <a href="/wiki/Eleven-plus" title="Eleven-plus">eleven-plus</a> standardized tests given in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1988_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1988-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Britannica introduced the <i>Children's Britannica</i> to the US market in 1988, aimed at ages seven to 14.
</p><p>In 1961, a 16 volume <i>Young Children's Encyclopaedia</i> was issued for children just learning to read.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1988_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1988-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>My First Britannica</i> is aimed at children ages six to 12, and the <i>Britannica Discovery Library</i> is for children aged three to six (issued 1974 to 1991).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There have been, and are, several abridged <i>Britannica</i> encyclopaedias. The single-volume <i>Britannica Concise Encyclopædia</i> has 28,000 short articles condensing the larger 32-volume <i>Britannica</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> there are authorized translations in languages such as <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a><sup id="cite_ref-TTO_Pham_Hong_Quan_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTO_Pham_Hong_Quan-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TTO_English_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTO_English-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TTO_Nguyen_Viet_Long_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTO_Nguyen_Viet_Long-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> <i>Compton's by Britannica</i>, first published in 2007, incorporating the former <i><a href="/wiki/Compton%27s_Encyclopedia" title="Compton&#39;s Encyclopedia">Compton's Encyclopedia</a></i>, is aimed at 10- to 17-year-olds and consists of 26 volumes and 11,000 pages.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1938, <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica,_Inc." title="Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.">Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.</a> has published annually a <i>Book of the Year</i> covering the past year's events. A given edition of the <i>Book of the Year</i> is named in terms of the year of its publication, though the edition actually covers the events of the previous year. Articles dating back to the 1994 edition are included online.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Cite is an example search, says nothing about what articles are available online. (August 2018)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The company also publishes several specialized reference works, such as <i>Shakespeare: The Essential Guide to the Life and Works of the Bard</i> (Wiley, 2006).
</p>
<h3><span id="Optical_disc.2C_online.2C_and_mobile_versions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Optical_disc,_online,_and_mobile_versions">Optical disc, online, and mobile versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Optical disc, online, and mobile versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Britannica_Ultimate_Reference_Suite" class="mw-redirect" title="Britannica Ultimate Reference Suite">Britannica Ultimate Reference Suite</a> 2012 DVD</i> contains over 100,000 articles.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> This includes regular <i>Britannica</i> articles, as well as others drawn from the <i>Britannica Student Encyclopædia</i>, and the <i>Britannica Elementary Encyclopædia.</i> The package includes a range of supplementary content including maps, videos, sound clips, animations and web links. It also offers study tools and dictionary and thesaurus entries from <a href="/wiki/Merriam-Webster" title="Merriam-Webster">Merriam-Webster</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica_Online" title="Encyclopædia Britannica Online"><i>Britannica</i> Online</a> is a website with more than 120,000 articles and is updated regularly.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2019)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It has daily features, updates and links to news reports from <i>The New York Times</i> and the <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC</a>. As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, roughly 60% of Encyclopædia Britannica's revenue came from online operations, of which around 15% came from subscriptions to the consumer version of the websites.<sup id="cite_ref-econsultancy_20090210_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econsultancy_20090210-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> As of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, subscriptions were available on a yearly, monthly or weekly basis.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Special subscription plans are offered to schools, colleges and libraries; such institutional subscribers constitute an important part of Britannica's business. Beginning in early 2007, the <i>Britannica</i> made articles freely available if they are hyperlinked from an external site. Non-subscribers are served pop-ups and advertising.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 February 2007, Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc. announced that it was working with mobile phone search company <a href="/wiki/AskMeNow" title="AskMeNow">AskMeNow</a> to launch a mobile encyclopaedia.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Users will be able to send a question via <a href="/wiki/Text_message" class="mw-redirect" title="Text message">text message</a>, and AskMeNow will search <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> 28,000-article concise encyclopaedia to return an answer to the query. Daily topical features sent directly to users' mobile phones are also planned.
</p><p>On 3 June 2008, an initiative to facilitate collaboration between online expert and amateur scholarly contributors for Britannica's online content (in the spirit of a <a href="/wiki/Wiki" title="Wiki">wiki</a>), with editorial oversight from Britannica staff, was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Approved contributions would be credited,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> though contributing automatically grants Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc. perpetual, irrevocable license to those contributions.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 January 2009, Britannica's president, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Cauz" title="Jorge Cauz">Jorge Cauz</a>, announced that the company would be accepting edits and additions to the online <i>Britannica</i> website from the public. The published edition of the encyclopaedia will not be affected by the changes.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Individuals wishing to edit the <i>Britannica</i> website will have to register under their real name and address prior to editing or submitting their content.<sup id="cite_ref-tg_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tg-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> All edits submitted will be reviewed and checked and will have to be approved by the encyclopaedia's professional staff.<sup id="cite_ref-tg_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tg-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Contributions from non-academic users will sit in a separate section from the expert-generated <i>Britannica</i> content,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> as will content submitted by non-<i>Britannica</i> scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-times_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Articles written by users, if vetted and approved, will also only be available in a special section of the website, separate from the professional articles.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-times_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Official <i>Britannica</i> material would carry a "Britannica Checked" stamp, to distinguish it from the user-generated content.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 September 2010, Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc. announced a partnership with mobile phone development company <a href="/wiki/Concentric_Sky" title="Concentric Sky">Concentric Sky</a> to launch a series of <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> products aimed at the <a href="/wiki/K%E2%80%9312_(education)" class="mw-redirect" title="K–12 (education)">K-12</a> market.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On 20 July 2011, Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc. announced that Concentric Sky had ported the Britannica Kids product line to Intel's <a href="/wiki/Intel_Atom" title="Intel Atom">Intel Atom</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Netbooks" class="mw-redirect" title="Netbooks">Netbooks</a><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and on 26 October 2011 that it had launched its encyclopedia as an <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a> <a href="/wiki/Application_software" title="Application software">app</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Britannica released Britannica ImageQuest, a database of images.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2012, it was announced that the company would cease printing the encyclopaedia set, and that it would focus more on its online version.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 June 2018, Britannica released a <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome_extension" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Chrome extension">Google Chrome extension</a>, Britannica Insights, which shows snippets of information from Britannica Online in a sidebar for <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google search</a> results.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The Britannica sidebar does not replace Google's sidebar and is instead placed above Google's sidebar.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel_and_management">Personnel and management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Personnel and management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contributors">Contributors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Contributors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 2007 print version of the <i>Britannica</i> has 4,411 contributors, many eminent in their fields, such as Nobel laureate economist <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a>, astronomer <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sagan" title="Carl Sagan">Carl Sagan</a>, and surgeon <a href="/wiki/Michael_DeBakey" title="Michael DeBakey">Michael DeBakey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-macropaedia_contributors_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macropaedia_contributors-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Roughly a quarter of the contributors are deceased, some as long ago as 1947 (<a href="/wiki/Alfred_North_Whitehead" title="Alfred North Whitehead">Alfred North Whitehead</a>), while another quarter are retired or <a href="/wiki/Emeritus" title="Emeritus">emeritus</a>. Most (approximately 98%<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>) contribute to only a single article; however, 64 contributed to three articles, 23 contributed to four articles, 10 contributed to five articles, and 8 contributed to more than five articles. An exceptionally prolific contributor is <a href="/wiki/Christine_Sutton" title="Christine Sutton">Christine Sutton</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>, who contributed 24 articles on <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">particle physics</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>While <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> authors have included writers such as <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marie_Curie" title="Marie Curie">Marie Curie</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Leon Trotsky</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> as well as notable independent encyclopaedists such as <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov">Isaac Asimov</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> some have been criticized for lack of expertise. In 1911 the historian <a href="/wiki/George_Lincoln_Burr" title="George Lincoln Burr">George L. Burr</a> wrote:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>With a temerity almost appalling, [the <i>Britannica</i> contributor, Mr. Philips] ranges over nearly the whole field of European history, political, social, ecclesiastical... The grievance is that &#91;this work&#93; lacks authority. This, too—this reliance on editorial energy instead of on ripe special learning—may, alas, be also counted an "Americanizing": for certainly nothing has so cheapened the scholarship of our American encyclopaedias.<sup id="cite_ref-burr_1911_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burr_1911-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Staff">Staff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Staff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Spencer_Baynes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Thomas_Spencer_Baynes.jpg/220px-Thomas_Spencer_Baynes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="289" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Thomas_Spencer_Baynes.jpg/330px-Thomas_Spencer_Baynes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Thomas_Spencer_Baynes.jpg/440px-Thomas_Spencer_Baynes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="608" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Spencer_Baynes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portrait of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Spencer_Baynes" title="Thomas Spencer Baynes">Thomas Spencer Baynes</a>, editor of the 9th edition. Painted in 1888, it now hangs in the Senate Room of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews" title="University of St Andrews">University of St Andrews</a> in Scotland.</div></div></div>
<p>As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> in the fifteenth edition of <i>Britannica</i>, <a href="/wiki/Dale_Hoiberg" title="Dale Hoiberg">Dale Hoiberg</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Sinology" title="Sinology">sinologist</a>, was listed as <i>Britannica's</i> Senior Vice President and editor-in-chief.<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_staff_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_staff-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Among his predecessors as editors-in-chief were <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Chisholm" title="Hugh Chisholm">Hugh Chisholm</a> (1902–1924), <a href="/wiki/James_Louis_Garvin" title="James Louis Garvin">James Louis Garvin</a> (1926–1932), <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Henry_Hooper" title="Franklin Henry Hooper">Franklin Henry Hooper</a> (1932–1938),<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Walter_Yust" title="Walter Yust">Walter Yust</a> (1938–1960), <a href="/wiki/Harry_Ashmore" title="Harry Ashmore">Harry Ashmore</a> (1960–1963), <a href="/wiki/Warren_E._Preece" title="Warren E. Preece">Warren E. Preece</a> (1964–1968, 1969–1975), Sir <a href="/wiki/William_Haley" title="William Haley">William Haley</a> (1968–1969), <a href="/wiki/Philip_W._Goetz" title="Philip W. Goetz">Philip W. Goetz</a> (1979–1991),<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_McHenry" title="Robert McHenry">Robert McHenry</a> (1992–1997).<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_History_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_History-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> Anita Wolff was listed as the Deputy Editor and <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Pappas" title="Theodore Pappas">Theodore Pappas</a> as Executive Editor.<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_staff_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_staff-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Prior Executive Editors include John V. Dodge (1950–1964) and Philip W. Goetz.
</p><p>Paul T. Armstrong remains the longest working employee of Encyclopædia Britannica. He began his career there in 1934, eventually earning the positions of Treasurer, Vice President, and Chief Financial Officer in his 58 years with the company, before retiring in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2007 editorial staff of the <i>Britannica</i> included five Senior Editors and nine Associate Editors, supervised by <a href="/wiki/Dale_Hoiberg" title="Dale Hoiberg">Dale Hoiberg</a> and four others. The editorial staff helped to write the articles of the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Microp%C3%A6dia" title="Micropædia">Micropædia</a></i> and some sections of the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Macrop%C3%A6dia" title="Macropædia">Macropædia</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_biochemistry_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB_biochemistry-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The preparation and publication of the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i> required trained staff. According to the final page of the 2007 <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Prop%C3%A6dia" title="Propædia">Propædia</a></i>, the staff were organized into ten departments:<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>Editorial staff (19 editors and 1 executive assistant)</li>
<li>Art and Cartography (9 employees)</li>
<li>Compositional Technology and Design (4 employees)</li>
<li>Copy Department (12 employees)</li>
<li>Editorial and Publishing Technologies (5 employees)</li>
<li>Information Management (9 employees)</li>
<li>Media Asset Management and Production Control (4 employees)</li>
<li>Reference Librarians (3 employees)</li>
<li>World Data (5 employees)</li>
<li>Manufacturing (1 employee)</li></ol>
<p>Some of these departments were organized <a href="/wiki/Hierarchy" title="Hierarchy">hierarchically</a>. For example, the copy editors were divided into four copy editors, two senior copy editors, four supervisors, plus a coordinator and a director. Similarly, the Editorial department was headed by <a href="/wiki/Dale_Hoiberg" title="Dale Hoiberg">Dale Hoiberg</a> and assisted by four others; they oversaw the work of five senior editors, nine associate editors, and one executive assistant.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Editorial_advisors">Editorial advisors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Editorial advisors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Britannica</i> has an Editorial Board of Advisors, which includes 12 distinguished scholars:<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_editorial_advisors_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_editorial_advisors-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> non-fiction author <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_G._Carr" title="Nicholas G. Carr">Nicholas Carr</a>, religion scholar <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Doniger" title="Wendy Doniger">Wendy Doniger</a>, political economist <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_M._Friedman" title="Benjamin M. Friedman">Benjamin M. Friedman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_on_Foreign_Relations" title="Council on Foreign Relations">Council on Foreign Relations</a> President Emeritus <a href="/wiki/Leslie_H._Gelb" title="Leslie H. Gelb">Leslie H. Gelb</a>, computer scientist <a href="/wiki/David_Gelernter" title="David Gelernter">David Gelernter</a>, Physics Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Murray_Gell-Mann" title="Murray Gell-Mann">Murray Gell-Mann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Corporation_of_New_York" title="Carnegie Corporation of New York">Carnegie Corporation of New York</a> President <a href="/wiki/Vartan_Gregorian" title="Vartan Gregorian">Vartan Gregorian</a>, philosopher <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Nagel" title="Thomas Nagel">Thomas Nagel</a>, cognitive scientist <a href="/wiki/Donald_Norman" class="mw-redirect" title="Donald Norman">Donald Norman</a>, musicologist <a href="/wiki/Don_Michael_Randel" title="Don Michael Randel">Don Michael Randel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Sutherland,_Baron_Sutherland_of_Houndwood" title="Stewart Sutherland, Baron Sutherland of Houndwood">Stewart Sutherland, Baron Sutherland of Houndwood</a>, President of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_Edinburgh" title="Royal Society of Edinburgh">Royal Society of Edinburgh</a>, and cultural anthropologist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wesch" title="Michael Wesch">Michael Wesch</a>.
</p><p>The <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Prop%C3%A6dia" title="Propædia">Propædia</a></i> and its <i>Outline of Knowledge</i> were produced by dozens of editorial advisors under the direction of <a href="/wiki/Mortimer_J._Adler" title="Mortimer J. Adler">Mortimer J. Adler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_other_editorial_advisors_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_other_editorial_advisors-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Roughly half of these advisors have since died, including some of the Outline's chief architects — <a href="/wiki/Rene_Dubos" class="mw-redirect" title="Rene Dubos">Rene Dubos</a> (d. 1982), <a href="/wiki/Loren_Eiseley" title="Loren Eiseley">Loren Eiseley</a> (d. 1977), <a href="/wiki/Harold_D._Lasswell" class="mw-redirect" title="Harold D. Lasswell">Harold D. Lasswell</a> (d. 1978), <a href="/wiki/Mark_Van_Doren" title="Mark Van Doren">Mark Van Doren</a> (d. 1972), <a href="/wiki/Peter_Ritchie_Calder" title="Peter Ritchie Calder">Peter Ritchie Calder</a> (d. 1982) and <a href="/wiki/Mortimer_J._Adler" title="Mortimer J. Adler">Mortimer J. Adler</a> (d. 2001). The <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Propædia</i> also lists just under 4,000 advisors who were consulted for the unsigned <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Microp%C3%A6dia" title="Micropædia">Micropædia</a></i> articles.<sup id="cite_ref-micropaedia_consultants_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-micropaedia_consultants-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_structure">Corporate structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Corporate structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 1996, the <i>Britannica</i> was purchased from the <a href="/wiki/Benton_Foundation" title="Benton Foundation">Benton Foundation</a> by billionaire Swiss financier <a href="/wiki/Jacqui_Safra" title="Jacqui Safra">Jacqui Safra</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> who serves as its current Chair of the Board. In 1997, Don Yannias, a long-time associate and investment advisor of Safra, became CEO of Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In 1999, a new company, <a href="/wiki/Britannica.com_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Britannica.com Inc.">Britannica.com Inc.</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Corporate_spin-off" title="Corporate spin-off">created</a> to develop digital versions of the <i>Britannica</i>; Yannias assumed the role of CEO in the new company, while his former position at the parent company remained vacant for two years. Yannias' tenure at Britannica.com Inc. was marked by missteps, considerable lay-offs, and financial losses.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, Yannias was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Ilan_Yeshua" title="Ilan Yeshua">Ilan Yeshua</a>, who reunited the leadership of the two companies.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Yannias later returned to investment management, but remains on the <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> Board of Directors.
</p><p>In 2003, former management consultant <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Aguilar-Cauz" class="mw-redirect" title="Jorge Aguilar-Cauz">Jorge Aguilar-Cauz</a> was appointed President of Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc. Cauz is the senior executive and reports directly to the <i>Britannica's</i> Board of Directors. Cauz has been pursuing alliances with other companies and extending the <i>Britannica</i> brand to new educational and reference products, continuing the strategy pioneered by former CEO <a href="/wiki/Elkan_Harrison_Powell" title="Elkan Harrison Powell">Elkan Harrison Powell</a> in the mid-1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_Chair_President_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_Chair_President-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Under Safra's ownership, the company has experienced financial difficulties and has responded by reducing the price of its products and implementing drastic cost cuts. According to a 2003 report in the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">New York Post</a></i>, the <i>Britannica</i> management has eliminated employee <a href="/wiki/401(k)" title="401(k)">401(k)</a> accounts and encouraged the use of free images. These changes have had negative impacts, as freelance contributors have waited up to six months for checks and the <i>Britannica</i> staff have gone years without pay rises.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the fall of 2017, Karthik Krishnan was appointed global chief executive officer of the Encyclopædia Britannica Group. Krishnan brought a varied perspective to the role based on several high-level positions in digital media, including RELX (Reed Elsevier, FT SE 100) and Rodale, in which he was responsible for "driving business and cultural transformation and accelerating growth".<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Taking the reins of the company as it was preparing to mark its 250th anniversary and define the next phase of its digital strategy for consumers and K-12 schools, Krishnan launched a series of new initiatives in his first year.
</p><p>First was Britannica Insights,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> a free, downloadable software extension to the Google Chrome browser that served up edited, fact-checked Britannica information with queries on search engines such as Google, Yahoo, and Bing. Its purpose, the company said, was to "provide trusted, verified information" in conjunction with search results that were thought to be increasingly unreliable in the era of misinformation and "fake news."
</p><p>The product was quickly followed by Britannica School Insights, which provided similar content for subscribers to Britannica's online classroom solutions, and a partnership with YouTube<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> in which verified Britannica content appeared on the site as an antidote to user-generated video content that could be false or misleading. &#160;
</p><p>Krishnan, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.stern.nyu.edu/faculty/bio/karthik-krishnan">himself an educator</a> at New York University's Stern School of Business, believes in the "transformative power of education"<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and set steering the company toward solidifying its place among leaders in educational technology and supplemental curriculum. Krishnan aimed at providing more useful and relevant solutions to customer needs, extending and renewing Britannica's historical emphasis on "Utility",<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> which had been the watchword of its first edition in 1768.
</p><p>Krishnan also is active in civic affairs, with organizations such as the Urban Enterprise Initiative and Urban Upbound, whose board he serves on.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Competition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As the <i>Britannica</i> is a general encyclopaedia, it does not seek to compete with specialized encyclopaedias such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclopaedia_of_Mathematics" class="mw-redirect" title="Encyclopaedia of Mathematics">Encyclopaedia of Mathematics</a></i> or the <i><a href="/wiki/Dictionary_of_the_Middle_Ages" title="Dictionary of the Middle Ages">Dictionary of the Middle Ages</a></i>, which can devote much more space to their chosen topics. In its first years, the <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> main competitor was the general encyclopaedia of <a href="/wiki/Ephraim_Chambers" title="Ephraim Chambers">Ephraim Chambers</a> and, soon thereafter, <i><a href="/wiki/Rees%27s_Cyclop%C3%A6dia" title="Rees&#39;s Cyclopædia">Rees's Cyclopædia</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Taylor_Coleridge" title="Samuel Taylor Coleridge">Coleridge's</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Metropolitana" title="Encyclopædia Metropolitana">Encyclopædia Metropolitana</a></i>. In the 20th century, successful competitors included <i><a href="/wiki/Collier%27s_Encyclopedia" title="Collier&#39;s Encyclopedia">Collier's Encyclopedia</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_Americana" title="Encyclopedia Americana">Encyclopedia Americana</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/World_Book_Encyclopedia" title="World Book Encyclopedia">World Book Encyclopedia</a></i>. Nevertheless, from the 9th edition onwards, the <i>Britannica</i> was widely considered to have the greatest authority of any general English language encyclopaedia,<sup id="cite_ref-thomas_1992_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomas_1992-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> especially because of its broad coverage and eminent authors.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The print version of the <i>Britannica</i> was significantly more expensive than its competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the early 1990s, the <i>Britannica</i> has faced new challenges from digital information sources. The Internet, facilitated by the development of <a href="/wiki/Web_search_engine" title="Web search engine">search engines</a>, has grown into a common source of information for many people, and provides easy access to reliable original sources and expert opinions, thanks in part to initiatives such as <a href="/wiki/Google_Book_Search" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Book Search">Google Books</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>'s <a href="/wiki/MIT_OpenCourseWare" title="MIT OpenCourseWare">release of its educational materials</a> and the open <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Central" title="PubMed Central">PubMed Central</a> library of the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="National Library of Medicine">National Library of Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In general, the Internet tends to provide more current coverage than print media, due to the ease with which material on the Internet can be updated.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In rapidly changing fields such as science, technology, politics, culture and modern history, the <i>Britannica</i> has struggled to stay up-to-date, a problem first analysed systematically by its former editor <a href="/wiki/Walter_Yust" title="Walter Yust">Walter Yust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_1954_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB_1954-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Eventually, the <i>Britannica</i> turned to focus more on its online edition.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Print_encyclopaedias">Print encyclopaedias</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Print encyclopaedias">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i> has been compared with other print encyclopaedias, both qualitatively and quantitatively.<sup id="cite_ref-library_association_1996_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-library_association_1996-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> A well-known comparison is that of <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Kister" title="Kenneth Kister">Kenneth Kister</a>, who gave a qualitative and quantitative comparison of the <i>Britannica</i> with two comparable encyclopaedias, <i><a href="/wiki/Collier%27s_Encyclopedia" title="Collier&#39;s Encyclopedia">Collier's Encyclopedia</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_Americana" title="Encyclopedia Americana">Encyclopedia Americana</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> For the quantitative analysis, ten articles were selected at random—<a href="/wiki/Circumcision" title="Circumcision">circumcision</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_R._Drew" title="Charles R. Drew">Charles Drew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galileo" class="mw-redirect" title="Galileo">Galileo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Glass" title="Philip Glass">Philip Glass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heart_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Heart disease">heart disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/IQ" class="mw-redirect" title="IQ">IQ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panda_bear" class="mw-redirect" title="Panda bear">panda bear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_harassment" title="Sexual harassment">sexual harassment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shroud_of_Turin" title="Shroud of Turin">Shroud of Turin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>—and letter grades of A–D or F were awarded in four categories: coverage, accuracy, clarity, and recency. In all four categories and for all three encyclopaedias, the four average grades fell between <a href="/wiki/Grade_conversion" class="mw-redirect" title="Grade conversion">B− and B+</a>, chiefly because none of the encyclopaedias had an article on sexual harassment in 1994. In the accuracy category, the <i>Britannica</i> received one "D" and seven "A"s, <i>Encyclopedia Americana</i> received eight "A"s, and <i>Collier's</i> received one "D" and seven "A"s; thus, <i>Britannica</i> received an average score of 92% for accuracy to <i>Americana</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s 95% and <i>Collier's</i> 92%. In the timeliness category, <i>Britannica</i> averaged an 86% to <i>Americana'</i>s 90% and <i>Collier's</i> 85%.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_encyclopaedias_on_optical_media">Digital encyclopaedias on optical media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Digital encyclopaedias on optical media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The most notable competitor of the <i>Britannica</i> among CD/DVD-ROM digital encyclopaedias was <i><a href="/wiki/Encarta" title="Encarta">Encarta</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-seymour_2006_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seymour_2006-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> now discontinued, a modern, multimedia encyclopaedia that incorporated three print encyclopaedias: <i><a href="/wiki/Funk_%26_Wagnalls" title="Funk &amp; Wagnalls">Funk &amp; Wagnalls</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Collier%27s_Encyclopedia" title="Collier&#39;s Encyclopedia">Collier's</a></i> and the <i>New Merit Scholar's Encyclopedia</i>. <i>Encarta</i> was the top-selling multimedia encyclopaedia, based on total US retail sales from January 2000 to February 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Both occupied the same price range, with the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica_Ultimate_Reference_Suite" title="Encyclopædia Britannica Ultimate Reference Suite">2007 Encyclopædia Britannica Ultimate</a></i> CD or DVD costing US$40–50<sup id="cite_ref-2007EncartaPrice_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007EncartaPrice-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_Store_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_Store-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> and the Microsoft Encarta Premium 2007 DVD costing US$45.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_Store_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_Store-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Britannica</i> contains 100,000 articles and <i><a href="/wiki/Webster%27s_Dictionary" title="Webster&#39;s Dictionary">Merriam-Webster's Dictionary and Thesaurus</a></i> (US only), and offers Primary and Secondary School editions.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_Store_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_Store-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> <i>Encarta</i> contained 66,000 articles, a user-friendly Visual Browser, interactive maps, math, language and homework tools, a US and UK dictionary, and a youth edition.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_Store_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_Store-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Like <i>Encarta</i>, the <i>Britannica</i> has been criticized for being biased towards United States audiences; the United Kingdom-related articles are updated less often, maps of the United States are more detailed than those of other countries, and it lacks a UK dictionary.<sup id="cite_ref-seymour_2006_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seymour_2006-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Like the <i>Britannica</i>, <i>Encarta</i> was available online by subscription, although some content could be accessed free.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet_encyclopaedias">Internet encyclopaedias</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Internet encyclopaedias">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The dominant internet encyclopaedia and main alternative to <i>Britannica</i> is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tancer_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tancer-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Woodson_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Woodson-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The key differences between the two lie in accessibility; the model of participation they bring to an <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A9distes" title="Encyclopédistes">encyclopedic project</a>; their respective style sheets and editorial policies; relative ages; the number of subjects treated; the number of languages in which articles are written and made available; and their underlying economic models: unlike <i>Britannica</i>, Wikipedia is a not-for-profit and is not connected with traditional profit- and contract-based publishing distribution networks.
</p><p>The 699 printed <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Macrop%C3%A6dia" title="Macropædia">Macropædia</a></i> articles are generally written by identified contributors, and the roughly 65,000 printed <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Microp%C3%A6dia" title="Micropædia">Micropædia</a></i> articles are the work of the editorial staff and identified outside consultants. Thus, a <i>Britannica</i> article either has known authorship or a set of possible authors (the editorial staff). With the exception of the editorial staff, most of the <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> contributors are experts in their field—some are Nobel laureates.<sup id="cite_ref-macropaedia_contributors_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macropaedia_contributors-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> By contrast, the articles of Wikipedia are written by people of unknown degrees of expertise: most do not claim any particular expertise, and of those who do, many are anonymous and have no verifiable credentials.<sup id="cite_ref-Giles_Nature_study_2005_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Giles_Nature_study_2005-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> It is for this lack of institutional vetting, or certification, that former <i>Britannica</i> editor-in-chief Robert McHenry notes his belief that Wikipedia cannot hope to rival the <i>Britannica</i> in accuracy.<sup id="cite_ref-FBE_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FBE-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, the journal <i>Nature</i> chose articles from both websites in a wide range of science topics and sent them to what it called "relevant" field experts for peer review. The experts then compared the competing articles—one from each site on a given topic—side by side, but were not told which article came from which site. <i>Nature</i> got back 42 usable reviews.
</p><p>In the end, the journal found just eight serious errors, such as general misunderstandings of vital concepts: four from each site. It also discovered many factual errors, omissions or misleading statements: 162 in Wikipedia and 123 in <i>Britannica</i>, an average of 3.86 mistakes per article for Wikipedia and 2.92 for <i>Britannica</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Giles_Nature_study_2005_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Giles_Nature_study_2005-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Although <i>Britannica </i>was revealed as the more accurate encyclopedia, with fewer errors, <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica,_Inc." title="Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.">Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.</a> in its detailed 20-page rebuttal called <i>Nature'</i>s study flawed and misleading<sup id="cite_ref-fatally_flawed_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fatally_flawed-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> and called for a "prompt" retraction. It noted that two of the articles in the study were taken from a <i>Britannica</i> yearbook and not the encyclopaedia, and another two were from <i>Compton's Encyclopedia</i> (called the <i>Britannica Student Encyclopedia</i> on the company's website). The rebuttal went on to mention that some of the articles presented to reviewers were combinations of several articles, and that other articles were merely excerpts but were penalized for factual omissions. The company also noted that several of what <i>Nature</i> called errors were minor spelling variations, and that others were matters of interpretation. <i>Nature</i> defended its story and declined to retract, stating that, as it was comparing Wikipedia with the web version of <i>Britannica</i>, it used whatever relevant material was available on <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s website.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
Interviewed in February 2009, the managing director of <i>Britannica UK</i> said: <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Wikipedia is a fun site to use and has a lot of interesting entries on there, but their approach wouldn't work for <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i>. My job is to create more awareness of our very different approaches to publishing in the public mind. They're a chisel, we're a drill, and you need to have the correct tool for the job.<sup id="cite_ref-econsultancy_20090210_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econsultancy_20090210-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_and_popular_assessments">Critical and popular assessments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Critical and popular assessments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reputation">Reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reputation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EB1_Plate_003_lark_flower.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/EB1_Plate_003_lark_flower.gif/220px-EB1_Plate_003_lark_flower.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/EB1_Plate_003_lark_flower.gif/330px-EB1_Plate_003_lark_flower.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/EB1_Plate_003_lark_flower.gif/440px-EB1_Plate_003_lark_flower.gif 2x" data-file-width="2164" data-file-height="2968" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EB1_Plate_003_lark_flower.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Intaglio_printing" class="mw-redirect" title="Intaglio printing">copperplate</a> by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bell_(engraver)" title="Andrew Bell (engraver)">Andrew Bell</a> from the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="History of the Encyclopædia Britannica">1st edition</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Since the 3rd edition, the <i>Britannica</i> has enjoyed a popular and critical reputation for general excellence.<sup id="cite_ref-library_association_1996_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-library_association_1996-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The 3rd and the 9th editions were pirated for sale in the United States,<sup id="cite_ref-kogan_1958_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kogan_1958-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> beginning with <i><a href="/wiki/Dobson%27s_Encyclopaedia" class="mw-redirect" title="Dobson&#39;s Encyclopaedia">Dobson's Encyclopaedia</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> On the release of the 14th edition, <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine dubbed the <i>Britannica</i> the "Patriarch of the Library".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> In a related advertisement, naturalist <a href="/wiki/William_Beebe" title="William Beebe">William Beebe</a> was quoted as saying that the <i>Britannica</i> was "beyond comparison because there is no competitor."<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> References to the <i>Britannica</i> can be found throughout <a href="/wiki/English_literature" title="English literature">English literature</a>, most notably in one of Sir <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Conan_Doyle" title="Arthur Conan Doyle">Arthur Conan Doyle</a>'s favourite <a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes" title="Sherlock Holmes">Sherlock Holmes</a> stories, "<a href="/wiki/The_Red-Headed_League" title="The Red-Headed League">The Red-Headed League</a>". The tale was highlighted by the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_London" title="Lord Mayor of London">Lord Mayor of London</a>, Gilbert Inglefield, at the <a href="/wiki/Bicentennial_of_the_Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Bicentennial of the Encyclopædia Britannica">bicentennial of the <i>Britannica</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_bicentennial_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB_bicentennial-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i>Britannica</i> has a reputation for summarising knowledge.<sup id="cite_ref-thomas_1992_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomas_1992-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> To further their education, some people have devoted themselves to reading the entire <i>Britannica</i>, taking anywhere from three to 22 years to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-kogan_1958_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kogan_1958-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Fat%27h_Ali_Shah_Qajar" class="mw-redirect" title="Fat&#39;h Ali Shah Qajar">Fat'h Ali</a> became the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Shah of Persia</a> in 1797, he was given a set of the <i>Britannica's</i> 3rd edition, which he read completely; after this feat, he extended his royal title to include "Most Formidable Lord and Master of the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-EB_bicentennial_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB_bicentennial-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Writer <a href="/wiki/George_Bernard_Shaw" title="George Bernard Shaw">George Bernard Shaw</a> claimed to have read the complete 9th edition—except for the science articles<sup id="cite_ref-kogan_1958_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kogan_1958-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>—and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Evelyn_Byrd" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Evelyn Byrd">Richard Evelyn Byrd</a> took the <i>Britannica</i> as reading material for his five-month stay at the <a href="/wiki/South_Pole" title="South Pole">South Pole</a> in 1934, while <a href="/wiki/Philip_Beaver" title="Philip Beaver">Philip Beaver</a> read it during a sailing expedition. More recently, <a href="/wiki/A.J._Jacobs" class="mw-redirect" title="A.J. Jacobs">A.J. Jacobs</a>, an editor at <i><a href="/wiki/Esquire_(magazine)" title="Esquire (magazine)">Esquire</a></i> magazine, read the entire 2002 version of the 15th edition, describing his experiences in the well-received 2004 book, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Know-It-All:_One_Man%27s_Humble_Quest_to_Become_the_Smartest_Person_in_the_World" class="mw-redirect" title="The Know-It-All: One Man&#39;s Humble Quest to Become the Smartest Person in the World">The Know-It-All: One Man's Humble Quest to Become the Smartest Person in the World</a></i>. Only two people are known to have read two independent editions: the author <a href="/wiki/C._S._Forester" title="C. S. Forester">C. S. Forester</a><sup id="cite_ref-kogan_1958_100-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kogan_1958-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Amos_Urban_Shirk" title="Amos Urban Shirk">Amos Urban Shirk</a>, an American businessman who read the 11th and 14th editions, devoting roughly three hours per night for four and a half years to read the 11th.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Several editors-in-chief of the <i>Britannica</i> are likely to have read their editions completely, such as <a href="/wiki/William_Smellie_(encyclopedist)" title="William Smellie (encyclopedist)">William Smellie</a> (1st edition), <a href="/wiki/William_Robertson_Smith" title="William Robertson Smith">William Robertson Smith</a> (9th edition), and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Yust" title="Walter Yust">Walter Yust</a> (14th edition).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The CD/DVD-ROM version of the <i>Britannica</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica_Ultimate_Reference_Suite" title="Encyclopædia Britannica Ultimate Reference Suite">Encyclopædia Britannica Ultimate Reference Suite</a></i>, received the 2004 Distinguished Achievement Award from the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Educational_Publishers" title="Association of Educational Publishers">Association of Educational Publishers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> On 15 July 2009, <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i> was awarded a spot as one of "Top Ten Superbrands in the UK" by a panel of more than 2,000 independent reviewers, as reported by the BBC.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coverage_of_topics">Coverage of topics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Coverage of topics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Topics are chosen in part by reference to the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Prop%C3%A6dia" title="Propædia">Propædia</a></i> "Outline of Knowledge".<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_preface_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_preface-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The bulk of the <i>Britannica</i> is devoted to geography (26% of the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Macrop%C3%A6dia" title="Macropædia">Macropædia</a></i>), biography (14%), biology and medicine (11%), literature (7%), physics and astronomy (6%), religion (5%), art (4%), Western philosophy (4%), and law (3%).<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> A complementary study of the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Microp%C3%A6dia" title="Micropædia">Micropædia</a></i> found that geography accounted for 25% of articles, science 18%, social sciences 17%, biography 17%, and all other humanities 25%.<sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Writing in 1992, one reviewer judged that the "range, depth, and <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/catholicity" class="extiw" title="wikt:catholicity">catholicity</a> of coverage [of the <i>Britannica</i>] are unsurpassed by any other general Encyclopaedia."<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i>Britannica</i> does not cover topics in equivalent detail; for example, the whole of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> and most other religions is covered in a single <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Macrop%C3%A6dia" title="Macropædia">Macropædia</a></i> article, whereas 14 articles are devoted to Christianity, comprising nearly half of all religion articles.<sup id="cite_ref-macropaedia_2007_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macropaedia_2007-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> However, the <i>Britannica</i> has been lauded as the <i>least</i> biased of general Encyclopaedias marketed to Western readers<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and praised for its biographies of important women of all eras.<sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>It can be stated without fear of contradiction that the 15th edition of the <i>Britannica</i> accords non-Western cultural, social, and scientific developments more notice than any general English-language encyclopedia currently on the market.</p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite><a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Kister" title="Kenneth Kister">Kenneth Kister</a>, in <i>Kister's Best Encyclopedias</i> (1994)</cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_editorial_decisions">Criticism of editorial decisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Criticism of editorial decisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On rare occasions, the <i>Britannica </i>was criticized for its editorial choices. Given its roughly constant size, the encyclopaedia has needed to reduce or eliminate some topics to accommodate others, resulting in controversial decisions.
