The initial 15th edition (1974–1985) was faulted for having reduced or eliminated coverage of children's literature, <a href="/wiki/Military_decoration" class="mw-redirect" title="Military decoration">military decorations</a>, and the French poet <a href="/wiki/Joachim_du_Bellay" title="Joachim du Bellay">Joachim du Bellay</a>; editorial mistakes were also alleged, such as inconsistent sorting of Japanese biographies.<sup id="cite_ref-Newsweek_1974_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newsweek_1974-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Its elimination of the index was condemned, as was the apparently arbitrary division of articles into the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Microp%C3%A6dia" title="Micropædia">Micropædia</a></i> and <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Macrop%C3%A6dia" title="Macropædia">Macropædia</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15th_criticism_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15th_criticism-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Summing up, one critic called the initial 15th edition a "qualified failure...&#91;that&#93; cares more for juggling its format than for preserving."<sup id="cite_ref-Newsweek_1974_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newsweek_1974-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> More recently, reviewers from the <a href="/wiki/American_Library_Association" title="American Library Association">American Library Association</a> were surprised to find that most educational articles had been eliminated from the 1992 <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i>, along with the article on <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-library_association_1992_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-library_association_1992-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some very few <i>Britannica</i>-appointed contributors are mistaken. A notorious instance from the <i>Britannica's</i> early years is the rejection of <a href="/wiki/Newtonian_gravity" class="mw-redirect" title="Newtonian gravity">Newtonian gravity</a> by <a href="/wiki/George_Gleig" title="George Gleig">George Gleig</a>, the chief editor of the 3rd edition (1788–1797), who wrote that gravity was caused by the <a href="/wiki/Fire_(classical_element)" title="Fire (classical element)">classical element of fire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kogan_1958_100-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kogan_1958-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Britannica</i> has also staunchly defended a scientific approach to cultural topics, as it did with <a href="/wiki/William_Robertson_Smith" title="William Robertson Smith">William Robertson Smith</a>'s articles on religion in the 9th edition, particularly his article stating that the Bible was not historically accurate (1875).<sup id="cite_ref-kogan_1958_100-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kogan_1958-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_criticisms">Other criticisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other criticisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica_Eleventh_Edition#Notable_commentary_on_the_Eleventh_Edition" title="Encyclopædia Britannica Eleventh Edition">Encyclopædia Britannica Eleventh Edition §&#160;Notable commentary on the Eleventh Edition</a></div>
<p>The <i>Britannica</i> has received criticism, especially as editions become outdated. It is expensive to produce a completely new edition of the <i>Britannica</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> and its editors delay for as long as fiscally sensible (usually about 25 years).<sup id="cite_ref-encyclopaedia_1954_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopaedia_1954-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> For example, despite continuous revision, the 14th edition became outdated after 35 years (1929–1964). When American physicist <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Einbinder" title="Harvey Einbinder">Harvey Einbinder</a> detailed its failings in his 1964 book, <i>The Myth of the Britannica</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> the encyclopaedia was provoked to produce the 15th edition, which required 10 years of work.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It is still difficult to keep the <i>Britannica</i> current; one recent critic writes, "it is not difficult to find articles that are out-of-date or in need of revision", noting that the longer <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i> articles are more likely to be outdated than the shorter <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> articles.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Information in the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> is sometimes inconsistent with the corresponding <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i> article(s), mainly because of the failure to update one or the other.<sup id="cite_ref-library_association_1996_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-library_association_1996-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The bibliographies of the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i> articles have been criticized for being more out-of-date than the articles themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-library_association_1996_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-library_association_1996-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sader_1995_8-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sader_1995-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010 an inaccurate entry about the Irish civil war was discussed in the Irish press following a decision of the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Education_and_Skills_(Ireland)" title="Department of Education and Skills (Ireland)">Department of Education and Science</a> to pay for online access.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Writing about the 3rd edition (1788–1797), <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s chief editor <a href="/wiki/George_Gleig" title="George Gleig">George Gleig</a> observed that "perfection seems to be incompatible with the nature of works constructed on such a plan, and embracing such a variety of subjects."<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In March 2006, the <i>Britannica</i> wrote, "we in no way mean to imply that <i>Britannica</i> is error-free; we have never made such a claim."<sup id="cite_ref-fatally_flawed_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fatally_flawed-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The sentiment is expressed by its original editor, <a href="/wiki/William_Smellie_(encyclopedist)" title="William Smellie (encyclopedist)">William Smellie</a>:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047074">.mw-parser-output .smallcaps{font-variant:small-caps}</style><p><span class="smallcaps">With</span> regard to errors in general, whether falling under the denomination of mental, typographical or accidental, we are conscious of being able to point out a greater number than any critic whatever. Men who are acquainted with the innumerable difficulties attending the execution of a work of such an extensive nature will make proper allowances. To these we appeal, and shall rest satisfied with the judgment they pronounce.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>However, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Cauz" title="Jorge Cauz">Jorge Cauz</a> (president of Encyclopædia Britannica Inc.) asserted in 2012 that "<i>Britannica</i> [...] will always be factually correct."<sup id="cite_ref-nytstop_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytstop-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Houghton_Typ_705.71.363_Encyclopaedia_Britannica,_1771_-_title_page.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Houghton_Typ_705.71.363_Encyclopaedia_Britannica%2C_1771_-_title_page.jpg/220px-Houghton_Typ_705.71.363_Encyclopaedia_Britannica%2C_1771_-_title_page.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Houghton_Typ_705.71.363_Encyclopaedia_Britannica%2C_1771_-_title_page.jpg/330px-Houghton_Typ_705.71.363_Encyclopaedia_Britannica%2C_1771_-_title_page.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Houghton_Typ_705.71.363_Encyclopaedia_Britannica%2C_1771_-_title_page.jpg/440px-Houghton_Typ_705.71.363_Encyclopaedia_Britannica%2C_1771_-_title_page.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1081" data-file-height="1373" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Houghton_Typ_705.71.363_Encyclopaedia_Britannica,_1771_-_title_page.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Title page of the first edition of the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="History of the Encyclopædia Britannica">History of the Encyclopædia Britannica</a></div>
<p>Past owners have included, in chronological order, the Edinburgh, Scotland printers <a href="/wiki/Colin_Macfarquhar" title="Colin Macfarquhar">Colin Macfarquhar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bell_(engraver)" title="Andrew Bell (engraver)">Andrew Bell</a>, Scottish bookseller <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Constable" title="Archibald Constable">Archibald Constable</a>, Scottish publisher <a href="/wiki/A_%26_C_Black" title="A &amp; C Black">A &amp; C Black</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horace_Everett_Hooper" title="Horace Everett Hooper">Horace Everett Hooper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a> Roebuck and <a href="/wiki/William_Benton_(senator)" class="mw-redirect" title="William Benton (senator)">William Benton</a>.
</p><p>The present owner of Encyclopædia Britannica Inc. is <a href="/wiki/Jacqui_Safra" title="Jacqui Safra">Jacqui Safra</a>, a Swiss billionaire and actor. Recent advances in information technology and the rise of electronic encyclopaedias such as <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica_Ultimate_Reference_Suite" title="Encyclopædia Britannica Ultimate Reference Suite">Encyclopædia Britannica Ultimate Reference Suite</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Encarta" title="Encarta">Encarta</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a> have reduced the demand for print encyclopaedias.<sup id="cite_ref-web_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> To remain competitive, Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc. has stressed the reputation of the <i>Britannica</i>, reduced its price and production costs, and developed electronic versions on <a href="/wiki/CD-ROM" title="CD-ROM">CD-ROM</a>, DVD, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>. Since the early 1930s, the company has promoted spin-off reference works.<sup id="cite_ref-encyclopaedia_1954_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopaedia_1954-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Editions">Editions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Editions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Britannica</i> has been issued in 15 editions, with multi-volume supplements to the 3rd and 4th editions (see the <a href="#Edition_summary">Table</a> below). The 5th and 6th editions were reprints of the 4th, the 10th edition was only a supplement to the 9th, just as the 12th and 13th editions were supplements to the 11th. The 15th underwent massive re-organization in 1985, but the updated, current version is still known as the 15th. The 14th and 15th editions were edited every year throughout their runs, so that later printings of each were entirely different from early ones.
</p><p>Throughout history, the <i>Britannica</i> has had two aims: to be an excellent reference book, and to provide educational material.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_encyclopedia_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB_encyclopedia-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> In 1974, the 15th edition adopted a third goal: to systematize all human knowledge.<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_preface_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_preface-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The history of the <i>Britannica</i> can be divided into five eras, punctuated by changes in management, or re-organization of the dictionary.
</p>
<h4><span id="1768.E2.80.931826"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1768–1826">1768–1826</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 1768–1826">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rosetta_Stone.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Rosetta_Stone.jpg/220px-Rosetta_Stone.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="319" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Rosetta_Stone.jpg/330px-Rosetta_Stone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bf/Rosetta_Stone.jpg 2x" data-file-width="365" data-file-height="530" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rosetta_Stone.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The early 19th-century editions of <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i> included influential, original research such as <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Young_(scientist)" title="Thomas Young (scientist)">Thomas Young's</a> article on Egypt, which included the translation of the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_hieroglyphs" title="Egyptian hieroglyphs">hieroglyphs</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Rosetta_Stone" title="Rosetta Stone">Rosetta Stone</a> (pictured).</div></div></div>
<p>In the first era (1st–6th editions, 1768–1826), the <i>Britannica</i> was managed and published by its founders, <a href="/wiki/Colin_Macfarquhar" title="Colin Macfarquhar">Colin Macfarquhar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bell_(engraver)" title="Andrew Bell (engraver)">Andrew Bell</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Constable" title="Archibald Constable">Archibald Constable</a>, and by others. The <i>Britannica</i> was first published between December 1768<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> and 1771 in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> as the <i>Encyclopædia Britannica, or, A Dictionary of Arts and Sciences, compiled upon a New Plan</i>. In part, it was conceived in reaction to the French <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A9die" title="Encyclopédie">Encyclopédie</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Denis_Diderot" title="Denis Diderot">Denis Diderot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean_le_Rond_d%27Alembert" title="Jean le Rond d&#39;Alembert">Jean le Rond d'Alembert</a> (published 1751–72), which had been inspired by <a href="/wiki/Cyclop%C3%A6dia,_or_an_Universal_Dictionary_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Cyclopædia, or an Universal Dictionary of Arts and Sciences">Chambers's <i>Cyclopaedia</i></a> (first edition 1728). It went on sale December 10.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i>Britannica</i> of this period was primarily a Scottish enterprise, and it is one of the most enduring legacies of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Enlightenment" title="Scottish Enlightenment">Scottish Enlightenment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> In this era, the <i>Britannica</i> moved from being a three-volume set (1st edition) compiled by one young editor—<a href="/wiki/William_Smellie_(encyclopedist)" title="William Smellie (encyclopedist)">William Smellie</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>—to a 20-volume set written by numerous authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-KafkerLoveland2009_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KafkerLoveland2009-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Several other encyclopaedias competed throughout this period, among them editions of <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Rees" title="Abraham Rees">Abraham Rees</a>'s <i>Cyclopædia</i> and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Taylor_Coleridge" title="Samuel Taylor Coleridge">Coleridge's</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Metropolitana" title="Encyclopædia Metropolitana">Encyclopædia Metropolitana</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/David_Brewster" title="David Brewster">David Brewster</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Encyclop%C3%A6dia" title="Edinburgh Encyclopædia">Edinburgh Encyclopædia</a></i>.
</p>
<h4><span id="1827.E2.80.931901"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1827–1901">1827–1901</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 1827–1901">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the second era (7th–9th editions, 1827–1901), the <i>Britannica</i> was managed by the Edinburgh publishing firm <a href="/wiki/A_%26_C_Black" title="A &amp; C Black">A &amp; C Black</a>. Although some contributors were again recruited through friendships of the chief editors, notably <a href="/wiki/Macvey_Napier" title="Macvey Napier">Macvey Napier</a>, others were attracted by the <i>Britannica's</i> reputation. The contributors often came from other countries and included the world's most respected authorities in their fields. A general index of all articles was included for the first time in the 7th edition, a practice maintained until 1974.
</p><p>Production of the 9th edition was overseen by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Spencer_Baynes" title="Thomas Spencer Baynes">Thomas Spencer Baynes</a>, the first English-born editor-in-chief. Dubbed the "Scholar's Edition", the 9th edition is the most scholarly of all <i>Britannicas</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kogan_1958_100-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kogan_1958-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> After 1880, Baynes was assisted by <a href="/wiki/William_Robertson_Smith" title="William Robertson Smith">William Robertson Smith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> No biographies of living persons were included.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell" title="James Clerk Maxwell">James Clerk Maxwell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Huxley" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Huxley">Thomas Huxley</a> were special advisors on science.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> However, by the close of the 19th century, the 9th edition was outdated, and the <i>Britannica</i> faced financial difficulties.
</p>
<h4><span id="1901.E2.80.931973"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1901–1973">1901–1973</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 1901–1973">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EncycBrit1913.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/EncycBrit1913.jpg/220px-EncycBrit1913.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/EncycBrit1913.jpg/330px-EncycBrit1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7d/EncycBrit1913.jpg 2x" data-file-width="433" data-file-height="256" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EncycBrit1913.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>US advertisement for the 11th edition from the May 1913 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="National Geographic Magazine">National Geographic Magazine</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>In the third era (10th–14th editions, 1901–1973), the <i>Britannica</i> was managed by American businessmen who introduced <a href="/wiki/Direct_marketing" title="Direct marketing">direct marketing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Door-to-door" title="Door-to-door">door-to-door</a> sales. The American owners gradually simplified articles, making them less scholarly for a mass market. The 10th edition was a nine-volume supplement to the 9th, but the 11th edition was a completely new work, and is still praised for excellence; its owner, <a href="/wiki/Horace_Everett_Hooper" title="Horace Everett Hooper">Horace Hooper</a>, lavished enormous effort on its perfection.<sup id="cite_ref-kogan_1958_100-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kogan_1958-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When Hooper fell into financial difficulties, the <i>Britannica</i> was managed by <a href="/wiki/Sears_Roebuck" class="mw-redirect" title="Sears Roebuck">Sears Roebuck</a> for 18 years (1920–1923, 1928–1943). In 1932, the vice-president of Sears, <a href="/wiki/Elkan_Harrison_Powell" title="Elkan Harrison Powell">Elkan Harrison Powell</a>, assumed presidency of the <i>Britannica</i>; in 1936, he began the policy of continuous revision. This was a departure from earlier practice, in which the articles were not changed until a new edition was produced, at roughly 25-year intervals, some articles unchanged from earlier editions.<sup id="cite_ref-encyclopaedia_1954_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopaedia_1954-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Powell developed new educational products that built upon the <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s reputation.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shipping_box_for_the_encyclopedia_Britannica_2013-04-13_12-24.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A wooden crate reading &quot;THE / ENCYCLOPAEDIA / BRITANNICA / STANDARD OF THE WORLD / FOURTEENTH EDITION / BLUE CLOTH / BOOKS KEEP DRY&quot;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Shipping_box_for_the_encyclopedia_Britannica_2013-04-13_12-24.jpg/220px-Shipping_box_for_the_encyclopedia_Britannica_2013-04-13_12-24.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Shipping_box_for_the_encyclopedia_Britannica_2013-04-13_12-24.jpg/330px-Shipping_box_for_the_encyclopedia_Britannica_2013-04-13_12-24.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Shipping_box_for_the_encyclopedia_Britannica_2013-04-13_12-24.jpg/440px-Shipping_box_for_the_encyclopedia_Britannica_2013-04-13_12-24.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shipping_box_for_the_encyclopedia_Britannica_2013-04-13_12-24.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A wooden shipping crate for the 14th edition of the <i>Britannica</i></div></div></div>
<p>In 1943, Sears donated the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i> to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>. <a href="/wiki/William_Benton_(senator)" class="mw-redirect" title="William Benton (senator)">William Benton</a>, then a vice president of the University, provided the working capital for its operation. The stock was divided between Benton and the University, with the University holding an option on the stock.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Benton became Chairman of the Board and managed the <i>Britannica</i> until his death in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Benton set up the <a href="/wiki/Benton_Foundation" title="Benton Foundation">Benton Foundation</a>, which managed the <i>Britannica</i> until 1996. In 1968, near the end of this era, the <i>Britannica</i> celebrated <a href="/wiki/Bicentennial_of_the_Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Bicentennial of the Encyclopædia Britannica">its bicentennial</a>.
</p>
<h4><span id="1974.E2.80.931994"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1974–1994">1974–1994</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 1974–1994">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the fourth era (1974–94), the <i>Britannica</i> introduced its 15th edition, which was re-organized into three parts: the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Microp%C3%A6dia" title="Micropædia">Micropædia</a></i>, the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Macrop%C3%A6dia" title="Macropædia">Macropædia</a></i>, and the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Prop%C3%A6dia" title="Propædia">Propædia</a></i>. Under <a href="/wiki/Mortimer_J._Adler" title="Mortimer J. Adler">Mortimer J. Adler</a> (member of the Board of Editors of Encyclopædia Britannica since its inception in 1949, and its chair from 1974; director of editorial planning for the 15th edition of <i>Britannica</i> from 1965),<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> the <i>Britannica</i> sought not only to be a good reference work and educational tool, but to systematize all human knowledge. The absence of a separate index and the grouping of articles into parallel encyclopaedias (the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micro-</i> and <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i>) provoked a "firestorm of criticism" of the initial 15th edition.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15th_criticism_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15th_criticism-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In response, the 15th edition was completely re-organized and indexed for a re-release in 1985. This second version of the 15th edition continued to be published and revised until the 2010 print version. The official title of the 15th edition is the <i>New Encyclopædia Britannica</i>, although it has also been promoted as <i>Britannica 3</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 March 1976 the US <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a> entered an opinion and order enjoining Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc. from using: a) deceptive advertising practices in recruiting sales agents and obtaining sales leads, and b) deceptive sales practices in the door-to-door presentations of its sales agents.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="1994.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1994–present">1994–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 1994–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eb_advert_1898.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Eb_advert_1898.jpg/220px-Eb_advert_1898.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="339" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Eb_advert_1898.jpg/330px-Eb_advert_1898.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Eb_advert_1898.jpg/440px-Eb_advert_1898.jpg 2x" data-file-width="915" data-file-height="1408" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eb_advert_1898.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Advertisement for the 9th edition (1898)</div></div></div>
<p>In the fifth era (1994–present), digital versions have been developed and released on <a href="/wiki/Optical_disc" title="Optical disc">optical media</a> and online. In 1996, the <i>Britannica</i> was bought by <a href="/wiki/Jacqui_Safra" title="Jacqui Safra">Jacqui Safra</a> at well below its estimated value, owing to the company's financial difficulties. <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica,_Inc." title="Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.">Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.</a> split in 1999. One part retained the company name and developed the print version, and the other, <a href="/wiki/Britannica.com_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Britannica.com Inc.">Britannica.com Inc.</a>, developed digital versions. Since 2001, the two companies have shared a CEO, <a href="/wiki/Ilan_Yeshua" title="Ilan Yeshua">Ilan Yeshua</a>, who has continued Powell's strategy of introducing new products with the <i>Britannica</i> name. In March 2012, Britannica's president, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Cauz" title="Jorge Cauz">Jorge Cauz</a>, announced that it would not produce any new print editions of the encyclopaedia, with the 2010 15th edition being the last. The company will focus only on the online edition and other educational tools.<sup id="cite_ref-nytstop_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytstop-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnn-stop_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-stop-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s final print edition was in 2010, a 32-volume set.<sup id="cite_ref-nytstop_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytstop-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> <i>Britannica Global Edition</i> was also printed in 2010. It contained 30 volumes and 18,251 pages, with 8,500 photographs, maps, flags, and illustrations in smaller "compact" volumes. It contained over 40,000 articles written by scholars from across the world, including Nobel Prize winners. Unlike the 15th edition, it did not contain <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macro-</i> and <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> sections, but ran A through Z as all editions up to the 14th had. The following is <i>Britannica</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s description of the work:<sup id="cite_ref-store.britannica.com_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-store.britannica.com-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The editors of <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i>, the world standard in reference since 1768, present the <i>Britannica Global Edition</i>. Developed specifically to provide comprehensive and global coverage of the world around us, this unique product contains thousands of timely, relevant, and essential articles drawn from the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Encyclopædia Britannica</i> itself, as well as from the <i>Britannica Concise Encyclopedia</i>, the <i>Britannica Encyclopedia of World Religions</i>, and Compton's by Britannica. Written by international experts and scholars, the articles in this collection reflect the standards that have been the hallmark of the leading English-language encyclopedia for over 240 years.
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dedications">Dedications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Dedications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Britannica</i> was <a href="/wiki/Dedication_(publishing)" title="Dedication (publishing)">dedicated</a> to the reigning <a href="/wiki/British_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="British monarchy">British monarch</a> from 1788 to 1901 and then, upon its sale to an American partnership, to the British monarch and the President of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Thus, the 11th edition is "dedicated by Permission to His Majesty <a href="/wiki/George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="George V of the United Kingdom">George the Fifth</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Great Britain and Ireland">King of Great Britain and Ireland</a> and of the British Dominions beyond the Seas, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_India" title="Emperor of India">Emperor of India</a>, and to <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">William Howard Taft</a>, President of the United States of America."<sup id="cite_ref-EB_1911_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB_1911-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The order of the dedications has changed with the relative power of the United States and Britain, and with relative sales; the 1954 version of the 14th edition is "Dedicated by Permission to the Heads of the Two English-Speaking Peoples, <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight David Eisenhower</a>, President of the United States of America, and Her Majesty, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth the Second</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-EB_1954_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB_1954-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Consistent with this tradition, the 2007 version of the current 15th edition was "dedicated by permission to the current President of the United States of America, <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, and Her Majesty, Queen Elizabeth II",<sup id="cite_ref-propedia_3_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia_3-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> while the 2010 version of the current 15th edition is "dedicated by permission to <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, President of the United States of America, and Her Majesty Queen Elizabeth II."<sup id="cite_ref-propedia2010_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propedia2010-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Edition_summary">Edition summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Edition summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td>Many long articles were copied from the 7th edition; 344 contributors including <a href="/wiki/William_Thomson,_1st_Baron_Kelvin" title="William Thomson, 1st Baron Kelvin">William Thomson</a>; authorized American sets printed by Little, Brown in Boston; 8,000 sets sold altogether
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="text-align:right;">9th
</th>
<td>1875–1889
</td>
<td>24 volumes, plus a 499-page index volume labeled Volume 25
</td>
<td>55,000 authorized<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup> plus 500,000 pirated sets
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Spencer_Baynes" title="Thomas Spencer Baynes">Thomas Spencer Baynes</a> (1875–80); then <a href="/wiki/W._Robertson_Smith" class="mw-redirect" title="W. Robertson Smith">W.&#160;Robertson Smith</a>
</td>
<td>Some carry-over from 8th edition, but mostly a new work; high point of scholarship; 10,000 sets sold by Britannica and 45,000 authorized sets made in the US by Little, Brown in Boston and Schribners' Sons in NY, but pirated widely (500,000 sets) in the US.<sup><a href="#editionnote3">3</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="text-align:right;">10th,<br />supplement to&#160;9th
</th>
<td>1902–1903
</td>
<td>11 volumes, plus the 24 volumes of the 9th. Volume 34 containing 124 detailed country maps with index of 250,000 names <sup><a href="#editionnote4">4</a></sup>
</td>
<td>70,000
</td>
<td>Sir <a href="/wiki/Donald_Mackenzie_Wallace" title="Donald Mackenzie Wallace">Donald Mackenzie Wallace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Chisholm" title="Hugh Chisholm">Hugh Chisholm</a> in London; <a href="/wiki/Arthur_T._Hadley" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthur T. Hadley">Arthur T. Hadley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Henry_Hooper" title="Franklin Henry Hooper">Franklin Henry Hooper</a> in New York City
</td>
<td>American partnership bought EB rights on 9 May 1901; high-pressure sales methods
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="text-align:right;"><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica_Eleventh_Edition" title="Encyclopædia Britannica Eleventh Edition">11th</a>
</th>
<td>1910–1911</td>
<td>28 volumes, plus volume 29 index
</td>
<td>1,000,000
</td>
<td>Hugh Chisholm in London, Franklin Henry Hooper in New York City
</td>
<td>Another high point of scholarship and writing; more articles than the 9th, but shorter and simpler; financial difficulties for owner, <a href="/wiki/Horace_Everett_Hooper" title="Horace Everett Hooper">Horace Everett Hooper</a>; EB rights sold to <a href="/wiki/Sears,_Roebuck_and_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Sears, Roebuck and Company">Sears Roebuck</a> in 1920
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="text-align:right;">12th,<br />supplement to&#160;11th
</th>
<td>1921–1922
</td>
<td>3 volumes with own index, plus the 29 volumes of the 11th<sup><a href="#editionnote5">5</a></sup>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>Hugh Chisholm in London, Franklin Henry Hooper in New York City
</td>
<td>Summarized state of the world before, during, and after World War I
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="text-align:right;">13th,<br />supplement to&#160;11th
</th>
<td>1926
</td>
<td>3 volumes with own index, plus the 29 volumes of the 11th<sup><a href="#editionnote6">6</a></sup>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/James_Louis_Garvin" title="James Louis Garvin">James Louis Garvin</a> in London, Franklin Henry Hooper in New York City
</td>
<td>Replaced 12th edition volumes; improved perspective of the events of 1910–1926
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="text-align:right;">14th
</th>
<td>1929–1933
</td>
<td>24 volumes <sup><a href="#editionnote7">7</a></sup>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/James_Louis_Garvin" title="James Louis Garvin">James Louis Garvin</a> in London, Franklin Henry Hooper in New York City
</td>
<td>Publication just before Great Depression was financially catastrophic<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="text-align:right;">revised 14th
</th>
<td>1933–1973
</td>
<td>24 volumes <sup><a href="#editionnote7">7</a></sup>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>Franklin Henry Hooper until 1938; then <a href="/wiki/Walter_Yust" title="Walter Yust">Walter Yust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Ashmore" title="Harry Ashmore">Harry Ashmore</a>, Warren E. Preece, William Haley
</td>
<td>Began continuous revision in 1936: every article revised at least twice every decade
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="text-align:right;" rowspan="2">15th
</th>
<td>1974–1984
</td>
<td>30 volumes <sup><a href="#editionnote8">8</a></sup>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>Warren E. Preece, then Philip W. Goetz
</td>
<td>Introduced three-part structure; division of articles into <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Microp%C3%A6dia" title="Micropædia">Micropædia</a></i> and <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Macrop%C3%A6dia" title="Macropædia">Macropædia</a></i>; <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Prop%C3%A6dia" title="Propædia">Propædia</a></i> Outline of Knowledge; separate index eliminated
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>1985–2010</td>
<td>32 volumes <sup><a href="#editionnote9">9</a></sup>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>Philip W. Goetz, then <a href="/wiki/Robert_McHenry" title="Robert McHenry">Robert McHenry</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Dale_Hoiberg" title="Dale Hoiberg">Dale Hoiberg</a>
</td>
<td>Restored two-volume index; some <i>Micropædia </i>and<i> Macropædia</i> articles merged; slightly longer overall; new versions were issued every few years. This edition is the last printed edition.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<table border="0" cellpadding="2">

<tbody><tr>
<td class="toccolours"><b>Edition notes</b>
<p><sup id="editionnote1">1</sup><i>Supplement to the fourth, fifth, and sixth editions of the Encyclopædia Britannica. With preliminary dissertations on the history of the sciences.</i>
</p><p><sup id="editionnote2">2</sup> The 7th to 14th editions included a separate index volume.
</p><p><sup id="editionnote3">3</sup> The 9th edition featured articles by notables of the day, such as <a href="/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell" title="James Clerk Maxwell">James Clerk Maxwell</a> on electricity and magnetism, and <a href="/wiki/William_Thomson,_1st_Baron_Kelvin" title="William Thomson, 1st Baron Kelvin">William Thomson</a> (who became Lord Kelvin) on heat.
</p><p><sup id="editionnote4">4</sup> The 10th edition included a maps volume and a cumulative index volume for the 9th and 10th edition volumes: <i>the new volumes, constituting, in combination with the existing volumes of the 9th ed., the 10th ed.&#160;... and also supplying a new, distinctive, and independent library of reference dealing with recent events and developments</i>
</p><p><sup id="editionnote5">5</sup> <i>Vols. 30–32&#160;... the New volumes constituting, in combination with the twenty-nine volumes of the eleventh edition, the twelfth edition</i>
</p><p><sup id="editionnote6">6</sup> This supplement replaced the previous supplement: <i>The three new supplementary volumes constituting, with the volumes of the latest standard edition, the thirteenth edition.</i>
</p><p><sup id="editionnote7">7</sup> At this point <i>Encyclopædia Britannica</i> began almost annual revisions. New revisions of the 14th edition appeared every year between 1929 and 1973 with the exceptions of 1931, 1934 and 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-145">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><sup id="editionnote8">8</sup> Annual revisions were published every year between 1974 and 2007 with the exceptions of 1996, 1999, 2000, 2004 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-145">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The 15th edition (introduced as "Britannica 3") was published in three parts: a 10-volume <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> (which contained short articles and served as an index), a 19-volume <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i>, plus the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Propædia</i> (see text).
</p><p><sup id="editionnote9">9</sup> In 1985, the system was modified by adding a separate two-volume index; the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i> articles were further consolidated into fewer, larger ones (for example, the previously separate articles about the 50 US states were all included into the "United States of America" article), with some medium-length articles moved to the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i>. The <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Micropædia</i> had 12 vols. and the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Macropædia</i> 17.
</p><p>The first CD-ROM edition was issued in 1994. At that time also an online version was offered for paid subscription. In 1999 this was offered free, and no revised print versions appeared. The experiment was ended in 2001 and a new printed set was issued in 2001.
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table>

<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-112">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Kister, the initial 15th edition (1974) required over $32 million to produce.<sup id="cite_ref-kister_1994_6-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kister_1994-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-137"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-137">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vol. I has (viii), 697, (i) pages, but 10 unpaginated pages are added between pages 586 and 587. Vol. II has (iii), 1009, (ii) pages, but page numbers 175-176 as well as page numbers 425-426 were used twice; additionally page numbers 311-410 were not used. Vol. III has (iii), 953, (i) pages, but page numbers 679-878 were not used.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKafkerLoveland200922_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKafkerLoveland200922-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-139"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-139">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Archibald Constable estimated in 1812 that there had been 3,500 copies printed, but revised his estimate to 3,000 in 1821.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKafkerLoveland200958_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKafkerLoveland200958-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-141"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-141">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Smellie, it was 10,000, as quoted by Robert Kerr in his "Memoirs of William Smellie." Archibald Constable was quoted as saying the production started at 5,000 and concluded at 13,000.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-144"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-144">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">10,000 sets sold by Britannica plus 45,000 genuine American reprints by Scribner's Sons, and "several hundred thousand sets of mutilated and fraudulent 9th editions were sold..."<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Most sources estimate there were 500,000 pirated sets.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia">"Defense mechanism". <i>Encyclopædia Britannica</i>. <b>3</b> (15th ed.). <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica,_Inc." title="Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.">Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.</a> 2007. p.&#160;957.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Defense+mechanism&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica&amp;rft.pages=957&amp;rft.edition=15th&amp;rft.pub=Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica%2C+Inc.&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEncyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-encyclopaedia_1954-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-encyclopaedia_1954_13-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-encyclopaedia_1954_13-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-encyclopaedia_1954_13-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-encyclopaedia_1954_13-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia">"Encyclopaedia". <i>Encyclopædia Britannica</i> (14th ed.). 1954.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Encyclopaedia&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica&amp;rft.edition=14th&amp;rft.date=1954&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEncyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> Aside from providing an excellent summary of the <i>Britannica's</i> history and early spin-off products, this article also describes the life-cycle of a typical <i>Britannica</i> edition. A new edition typically begins with strong sales that decay as the encyclopaedia becomes outdated. When work on a new edition is begun, sales of the old edition stop, just when fiscal needs are greatest: a new editorial staff must be assembled, articles commissioned. <a href="/wiki/Elkan_Harrison_Powell" title="Elkan Harrison Powell">Elkan Harrison Powell</a> identified this fluctuation of income as a danger to any encyclopaedia, one he hoped to overcome with continuous revision.</span>
</li>
